<p><b>KK Partizan</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_language" title="Serbian Cyrillic language">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: <span lang="sr"><span class="Unicode">КК Партизан</span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbian</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">club</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>. It is part of the multi-sports <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>-based club <a href="/wiki/JSD_Partizan" title="JSD Partizan">Partizan</a>. The club competes in the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_League_of_Serbia" title="Basketball League of Serbia">KLS</a> and <a href="/wiki/ABA_League" title="ABA League">Adriatic League</a>.</p>
<p>Since 1945, Partizan has won around 45 trophies, and is the holder of the 21 national champion titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> They have also won 14 national basketball cups and 6 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adriatic_League" title="Adriatic League">Adriatic championships</a>, and notably the European Champion trophy at the Final Four of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euroleague" title="Euroleague">Euroleague</a> in Istanbul in 1992. KK Partizan was the <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">Euroleague Basketball</a> champion in 1992, playing all but one of the games (including the quarter-final game against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtus_Bologna" title="Virtus Bologna">Knorr Bologna</a>) on foreign grounds (in the <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Fuenlabrada" title="Fuenlabrada">Fuenlabrada</a>); <a href="/wiki/FIBA" title="FIBA">FIBA</a> decided not to allow teams from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SFR_Yugoslavia" title="SFR Yugoslavia">former Yugoslavia</a> to play their home games at their home venues, because of open hostilities in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Same year club took national championship and cup, and won <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_in_Basketball" title="Triple Crown in Basketball">Triple Crown</a>. KK Partizan was not allowed to defend the Euroleague title in the 1992–93 season, because of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_757" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 757">UN sanctions</a>. They also won 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kora%C4%87_Cup" title="Korać Cup">Korać Cups</a> in 1978, 1979 and 1989.</p>
<p>In September 2009, KK Partizan became the first Serbian team to play an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_versus_Euroleague_games" title="NBA versus Euroleague games">official game against NBA teams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1945.E2.80.931971:_formation_and_early_years">1945–1971: formation and early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1945–1971: formation and early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The club was founded on 4 October 1945, as a basketball section of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_People%27s_Army" title="Yugoslav People's Army">Sports Association of the Central House of the Yugoslav Army</a>. The first club championship of Yugoslavia was held in 1946, and the Partizan team consisted mostly of players from <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Army_(basketball_team)" title="Yugoslav Army (basketball team)">Yugoslav Army basketball team</a>, which in 1945 won the state championship tournament against teams of Yugoslav republics. KK Partizan officially ceased to be a club of the Army in 1953, since the entire sports society became independent and received the name of Partizan Yugoslav Sports Association (<a href="/wiki/JSD_Partizan" title="JSD Partizan">JSD Partizan</a>).</p>
<p>Although with a strong roster, including players who played for the national team of Yugoslavia, Partizan waited for the first senior title of Yugoslav champion until 1976. In the first 30 years of history players for Partizan have included <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mirko_Marjanovi%C4%87_(basketball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mirko Marjanović (basketball) (page does not exist)">Mirko Marjanović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bo%C5%BEidar_Mun%C4%87an&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Božidar Munćan (page does not exist)">Božidar Munćan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radomir_%C5%A0aper" title="Radomir Šaper">Radomir Šaper</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vilmo%C5%A1_Loci&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vilmoš Loci (page does not exist)">Vilmoš Loci</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lajo%C5%A1_Engler&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lajoš Engler (page does not exist)">Lajoš Engler</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C4%8Cedomir_Stoji%C4%8Devi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Čedomir Stojičević (page does not exist)">Čedomir Stojičević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borislav_Stankovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Stanković">Borislav Stanković</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Borislav_%C4%86ur%C4%8Di%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Borislav Ćurčić (page does not exist)">Borislav Ćurčić</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Branko_Radovi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Branko Radović (page does not exist)">Branko Radović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Radovan_Radovi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Radovan Radović (page does not exist)">Radovan Radović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Milo%C5%A1_Bojovi%C4%87_(basketball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miloš Bojović (basketball) (page does not exist)">Miloš Bojović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dragutin_%C4%8Cermak" title="Dragutin Čermak">Dragutin Čermak</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Slobodan_Jeli%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Slobodan Jelić (page does not exist)">Slobodan Jelić</a> and others. During this period Partizan finished five times as second-placed in the championship of Yugoslavia, and on two occasions it had the same number of points as the winner, but failed to reach the title of national champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1971.E2.80.931981">1971–1981</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1971–1981">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dalipagic.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="264" data-file-width="199" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Dalipagic.JPG/150px-Dalipagic.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b6/Dalipagic.JPG 1.5x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dalipagic.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Dalipagi%C4%87" title="Dražen Dalipagić">Dražen Dalipagić</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 1970s, when former players started to run the club and when the coaching job was taken by <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_basketball_team" title="Yugoslavia national basketball team">national team</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Ranko_%C5%BDeravica" title="Ranko Žeravica">Ranko Žeravica</a>. He made a great selection of young players led by <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Dalipagi%C4%87" title="Dražen Dalipagić">Dražen Dalipagić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Ki%C4%87anovi%C4%87" title="Dragan Kićanović">Dragan Kićanović</a>. Since Žeravica, as the national team coach (until 1965 as an assistant to <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Nikolić">Aleksandar Nikolić</a> and then as head coach) followed the development of international basketball for more than ten years, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">American professional league</a>, he tried to combine the best features of American and Soviet concepts of the game, while adapting them to the mentality of the Belgrade, Serbia and Yugoslav regions.</p>
<p>He gathered around him other young professionals, and in late 1970s, when Žeravica went coaching abroad, his former associates <a href="/wiki/Borislav_%C4%86orkovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Ćorković">Borislav Ćorković</a> and <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Ivkovi%C4%87" title="Dušan Ivković">Dušan Ivković</a> took over the team.</p>
<p>This period in the club's history included a few trophies. The first of these was the title of Yugoslav champion in 1975–76 season, followed by two victories in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kora%C4%87_Cup" title="Korać Cup">Korać Cup</a> (1978 in Banja Luka, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KK_Bosna" title="KK Bosna">KK Bosna</a> was defeated with 117–110, while in 1979 Partizan defeated Italian <a href="/wiki/Nuova_AMG_Sebastiani_Basket_Rieti" title="Nuova AMG Sebastiani Basket Rieti">Arrigoni</a> 108–98), first <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a> in 1978–79 and another national championship title in 1980–81. In addition to coaches Žeravica, Ćorković and Ivković, notable players included <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Dalipagi%C4%87" title="Dražen Dalipagić">Dražen Dalipagić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Ki%C4%87anovi%C4%87" title="Dragan Kićanović">Dragan Kićanović</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Dragutin_%C4%8Cermak" title="Dragutin Čermak">Dragutin Čermak</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Goran_Latifi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Goran Latifić (page does not exist)">Goran Latifić</a> (captain of the first championship team in 1976), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Josip_Far%C4%8Di%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Josip Farčić (page does not exist)">Josip Farčić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Todori%C4%87" title="Dragan Todorić">Dragan Todorić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Kerkez_(basketball)" title="Dušan Kerkez (basketball)">Dušan Kerkez</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miodrag_Mari%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miodrag Marić (page does not exist)">Miodrag Marić</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Boban_Petrovi%C4%87_(basketball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Boban Petrović (basketball) (page does not exist)">Boban Petrović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Arsenije_Pe%C5%A1i%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Arsenije Pešić (page does not exist)">Arsenije Pešić</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Boris_Beravs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Boris Beravs (page does not exist)">Boris Beravs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milenko_Savovi%C4%87" title="Milenko Savović">Milenko Savović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jadran_Vuja%C4%8Di%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jadran Vujačić (page does not exist)">Jadran Vujačić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neboj%C5%A1a_Zorki%C4%87" title="Nebojša Zorkić">Nebojša Zorkić</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_Ze%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Žarko Zečević">Žarko Zečević</a> and many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1985.E2.80.931991">1985–1991</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1985–1991">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a calm period due to a change of generations, by the end of the 1980s under the leadership of new club director, Dragan Kićanović involved young experts, such as <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a> (coaches in the mid 1980s were also <a href="/wiki/Zoran_Slavni%C4%87" title="Zoran Slavnić">Zoran Slavnić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borislav_D%C5%BEakovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Džaković">Borislav Džaković</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Lu%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Vladislav Lučić">Vladislav Lučić</a>).</p>
<p>The generation of <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_%C4%90or%C4%91evi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Đorđević">Aleksandar Đorđević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlade_Divac" title="Vlade Divac">Vlade Divac</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_Paspalj" title="Žarko Paspalj">Žarko Paspalj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Naki%C4%87" title="Ivo Nakić">Ivo Nakić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Pecarski" title="Miroslav Pecarski">Miroslav Pecarski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Popovi%C4%87" title="Oliver Popović">Oliver Popović</a> grew up, and with support of slightly older <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Željko Obradović">Željko Obradović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milenko_Savovi%C4%87" title="Milenko Savović">Milenko Savović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goran_Grbovi%C4%87" title="Goran Grbović">Goran Grbović</a>, led by young coach <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a>, brought Partizan back to the top of Yugoslav and European basketball.</p>
<p>That generation won the title of national champion in 1986–87, and in 1988, after victories in the Euroleague over European clubs including <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona_B%C3%A0squet" title="FC Barcelona Bàsquet">FC Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_B.C." title="Maccabi Tel Aviv B.C.">Maccabi Elite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aris_B.C." title="Aris B.C.">Aris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pallacanestro_Olimpia_Milano" title="Pallacanestro Olimpia Milano">Tracer Milano</a>) secured participation in the Final Four in the Belgian city of <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a>. After losing in the semifinals to Maccabi Tel Aviv (82–87), Partizan won over Aris (105–93) and won third place in Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="320" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg/150px-Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg/225px-Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg/300px-Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vlade_Divac_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vlade_Divac" title="Vlade Divac">Vlade Divac</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1989, enforced by young <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Danilovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Danilović">Predrag Danilović</a>, Partizan won the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Kora%C4%87_Cup" title="FIBA Korać Cup">FIBA Korać Cup</a> for the third time, triumphing over <a href="/wiki/Pallacanestro_Cant%C3%B9" title="Pallacanestro Cantù">Wiwa Vismara Cantù</a>. After losing the first game in Italy (76–89), Partizan celebrated the return leg in Belgrade with 101–82. That same season, Partizan won the Yugoslav Cup over new European champions <a href="/wiki/KK_Split" title="KK Split">Jugoplastika</a> (87–74).</p>
<p>European and worldwide recognition of this second generation of players attracted many talented young basketball players to the club, but at the same time, interest from financially powerful clubs in Europe and the United States for the best players significantly reduced their time spent in the club. <a href="/wiki/Vlade_Divac" title="Vlade Divac">Vlade Divac</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_Paspalj" title="Žarko Paspalj">Žarko Paspalj</a> in late 1989, along with <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Petrovi%C4%87" title="Dražen Petrović">Dražen Petrović</a> from <a href="/wiki/KK_Cibona" title="KK Cibona">Cibona</a> became the first players from the territory of Yugoslavia who pursued their careers in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA" title="NBA">NBA</a> league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1991.E2.80.931992">1991–1992</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1991–1992">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the departure of Divac, Paspalj, Grbović, Savović and other main players of the previous seasons, Partizan created a new young team for the 1991–92 season, notably <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_%C4%90or%C4%91evi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Đorđević">Aleksandar Đorđević</a> and <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Danilovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Danilović">Predrag Danilović</a>. For the new coach, management chose a team captain and former national team player with almost no coaching experience, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%BDelimir_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Želimir Obradović">Želimir Obradović</a>. His professional counselor became former Partizan coach and player, top European basketball expert, professor <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Nikolić">Aleksandar Nikolić</a>.</p>
<p>Obradović claimed that Partizan again had a very strong team, that the new tandem coaching of Đorđević and Danilović was the best <a href="/wiki/Basketball_positions" title="Basketball positions">backcourt pair</a> in Europe and that his team would not be an outsider in Euroleague.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/FIBA" title="FIBA">FIBA</a> decided not to allow teams from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_Yugoslavia" title="Former Yugoslavia">former Yugoslavia</a> to play their home games at their home venues, because of open hostilities in the region. Belgrade's "Black and Whites" have opted to be "hosts" in the <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Fuenlabrada" title="Fuenlabrada">Fuenlabrada</a>, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polideportivo_Fernando_Martin" title="Polideportivo Fernando Martin">Polideportivo Fernando Martin</a> arena.</p>
<p>Obradović's team began a long season of European and domestic matches, often traveling thousands of kilometers in just a few days, with performance gradually improving. Partizan finished the competition in the group stage in the Euroleague in fourth place with nine wins and five defeats. That meant that Partizan in crucial matches to qualify for the Final Four had to play with <a href="/wiki/Virtus_Pallacanestro_Bologna" title="Virtus Pallacanestro Bologna">Knorr Bologna</a>. Bolognese had a strong team led by former Yugoslav national team player <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jurij_Zdovc" title="Jurij Zdovc">Jurij Zdovc</a>. But Đorđević, Danilović, <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Naki%C4%87" title="Ivo Nakić">Ivo Nakić</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zoran_Stevanovi%C4%87_(basketball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zoran Stevanović (basketball) (page does not exist)">Zoran Stevanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Dragutinovi%C4%87" title="Vladimir Dragutinović">Vladimir Dragutinović</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Rebra%C4%8Da" title="Željko Rebrača">Željko Rebrača</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mla%C4%91an_%C5%A0ilobad" title="Mlađan Šilobad">Mlađan Šilobad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavi%C5%A1a_Koprivica" title="Slaviša Koprivica">Slaviša Koprivica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Lon%C4%8Dar" title="Nikola Lončar">Nikola Lončar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragi%C5%A1a_%C5%A0ari%C4%87" title="Dragiša Šarić">Dragiša Šarić</a> were better in three games and for the second time won the place in the Final Four. Partizan won the title of European champion, achieved on the Final Four in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> in April 1992. The average age of the team was 21.7, and out of 17 games all but one (the quarter-final game against <a href="/wiki/Virtus_Pallacanestro_Bologna" title="Virtus Pallacanestro Bologna">Knorr Bologna</a> in Belgrade) were played on foreign grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the Final Four held in <a href="/wiki/Abdi_%C4%B0pek%C3%A7i_Arena" title="Abdi İpekçi Arena">Abdi İpekçi Arena</a> in Istanbul Partizan defeated, at that moment the two strongest European teams – in the semifinals Italian <a href="/wiki/Pallacanestro_Olimpia_Milano" title="Pallacanestro Olimpia Milano">Philips Milano</a> and in finals Spanish <a href="/wiki/Joventut_Badalona" title="Joventut Badalona">Montigalà Joventut</a> (71–70), with three points in the last second by <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_%C4%90or%C4%91evi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Đorđević">Aleksandar Đorđević</a>. Partizan took the title of European champion. The season finished with victory in the national championship and Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1992.E2.80.931995">1992–1995</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1992–1995">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the Istanbul triumph Đorđević and Danilović moved to Italy. They went to clubs that Partizan defeated the year before during its "conquest of Europe" – Danilović in <a href="/wiki/Virtus_Pallacanestro_Bologna" title="Virtus Pallacanestro Bologna">Knorr</a> and Đorđević in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olimpia_Milano" title="Olimpia Milano">Phillips</a>. The departure of these two proved to be an irreparable loss. Because of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> sanctions against Yugoslavia, Partizan was not allowed to defend the European title in 1992–93 season. In 1992–93 season, led by coach <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Lukaji%C4%87" title="Željko Lukajić">Željko Lukajić</a> Partizan won the national cup, and the next season was again very successful. The team coached by <a href="/wiki/Borislav_D%C5%BEakovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Džaković">Borislav Džaković</a> won both domestic league and cup. The new generation of players included <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Lon%C4%8Dar" title="Nikola Lončar">Nikola Lončar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Beri%C4%87" title="Miroslav Berić">Miroslav Berić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haris_Brki%C4%87" title="Haris Brkić">Haris Brkić</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Rebra%C4%8Da" title="Željko Rebrača">Željko Rebrača</a>, <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Drobnjak" title="Predrag Drobnjak">Predrag Drobnjak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_%C4%8Cubrilo" title="Aleksandar Čubrilo">Aleksandar Čubrilo</a>. Additionally, in 1995 Yugoslav clubs were again able to compete in European competitions. Young players with no experience in Europe didn't achieve any significant results in their returning season in Europe, but under the guidance of Ranko Žeravica they took the national title in 1995–96 and secured another season in Europe's top competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996.E2.80.931998">1996–1998</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1996–1998">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1996–97 season Partizan, led by new coach <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Miroslav Nikolić">Miroslav Nikolić</a>, qualified for the Top 16 of Euroleague where it was eliminated by later European champion <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_B.C." title="Olympiacos B.C.">Olympiacos</a>. Partizan defended the title in domestic league with players including <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Toma%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Dejan Tomašević">Dejan Tomašević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Koturovi%C4%87" title="Dejan Koturović">Dejan Koturović</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Lukovski" title="Dragan Lukovski">Dragan Lukovski</a>. Next season, 1997–98, was a success in Euroleague. Two years after their "return to Europe" Partizan won the third participation in the Final Four. After a series of defeats in group stage, Miroslav Nikolić resigned and was replaced by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Milovan_Bogojevi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Milovan Bogojević (page does not exist)">Milovan Bogojević</a>. It eliminated the official champion <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_B.C." title="Olympiacos B.C.">Olympiacos</a>, and then in the quarterfinals it bested the Russian champions <a href="/wiki/PBC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PBC CSKA Moscow">CSKA</a>. After the departure of Berić and Koturović, enforced with new backcourt pair <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Rado%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Miroslav Radošević">Miroslav Radošević</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vladimir_%C4%90oki%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vladimir Đokić (page does not exist)">Vladimir Đokić</a> Partizan took fourth place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> However, the season in domestic competition was failure, and some players including <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Drobnjak" title="Predrag Drobnjak">Predrag Drobnjak</a> left the club.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1998.E2.80.932006">1998–2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1998–2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a disappointing domestic league ending, <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Lu%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Vladislav Lučić">Vladislav Lučić</a> was appointed as a new head coach of the club. The domestic 1998–99 season was not completed following the <a href="/wiki/NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" title="NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">NATO bombing of Yugoslavia</a>, but Partizan won the Yugoslav Cup, defeating <a href="/wiki/KK_FMP" title="KK FMP">KK FMP</a> in the finals, in a game that was played to the sound <a href="/wiki/Civil_defense_siren" title="Civil defense siren">civil defense sirens</a>. At the end of the season most of players left the club, and another young squad was formed. Led by coach <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nenad_Trajkovi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nenad Trajković (page does not exist)">Nenad Trajković</a> and players <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Rado%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Miroslav Radošević">Radоšević</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vladimir_%C4%90oki%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vladimir Đokić (page does not exist)">Đokić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_%C4%8Cubrilo" title="Aleksandar Čubrilo">Čubrilo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nenad_%C4%8Canak_(basketball)" title="Nenad Čanak (basketball)">Nenad Čanak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ratko_Varda" title="Ratko Varda">Ratko Varda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veselin_Petrovi%C4%87_(basketball)" title="Veselin Petrović (basketball)">Veselin Petrović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dragan_Markovi%C4%87_(basketball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dragan Marković (basketball) (page does not exist)">Dragan Marković</a> Partizan defended the Yugoslav Cup title. 2000–01 season was marked by the comeback of players <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Beri%C4%87" title="Miroslav Berić">Berić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Bulatovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Bulatović">Nikola Bulatović</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aleksandar_Glinti%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aleksandar Glintić (page does not exist)">Aleksandar Glintić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Branko_Milisavljevi%C4%87" title="Branko Milisavljević">Branko Milisavljević</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vlade_Divac" title="Vlade Divac">Vlade Divac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Danilovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Danilović">Predrag Danilović</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDarko_Paspalj" title="Žarko Paspalj">Žarko Paspalj</a> as part of the club management. The coach was <a href="/wiki/Darko_Ruso" title="Darko Ruso">Darko Ruso</a>, and Partizan managed the Top 16 of Euroleague.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In December 2000 <a href="/wiki/Haris_Brki%C4%87" title="Haris Brkić">Haris Brkić</a>, who returned to club just weeks earlier, was shot and killed outside of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pionir_Hall" title="Pionir Hall">Pionir Hall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1996" data-file-width="1894" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg/150px-Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg/225px-Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg/300px-Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a> is the most successful coach in club's history.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a> returned at the beginning of a rise in the fortunes of the club. Since the 2001–02 season, Partizan has been the most successful club in Serbia and the wider region, winning thirteen consecutive national titles, six national cups (five consecutive), and six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_ABA" title="Liga ABA">Adriatic league</a> titles (five consecutive) in the Euroleague.</p>
<p>Alongside the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina" title="University of North Carolina">University of North Carolina</a>, Partizan has provided the most NBA players since 1991, with five of them were selected in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/NBA_draft" title="NBA draft">NBA draft</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, the financial situation in Serbia makes it impossible to keep young players together for long, thus affecting clubs' chances of fighting on equal terms with more financially powerful European clubs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the period between 2001 and 2006 Partizan struggled with its results in Euroleague. On the domestic front Partizan was highly successful and built up for European success in following years. During these years, notable players from Partizan champion squads included <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Vujani%C4%87" title="Miloš Vujanić">Miloš Vujanić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nenad_Krsti%C4%87" title="Nenad Krstić">Nenad Krstić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vule_Avdalovi%C4%87" title="Vule Avdalović">Vule Avdalović</a>, young national team players <a href="/wiki/Uro%C5%A1_Tripkovi%C4%87" title="Uroš Tripković">Uroš Tripković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luka_Bogdanovi%C4%87" title="Luka Bogdanović">Luka Bogdanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosta_Perovi%C4%87" title="Kosta Perović">Kosta Perović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Baki%C4%87" title="Boris Bakić">Boris Bakić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Borovnjak" title="Dejan Borovnjak">Dejan Borovnjak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novica_Veli%C4%8Dkovi%C4%87" title="Novica Veličković">Novica Veličković</a>. They were supported by more experienced players like <a href="/wiki/Vlado_%C5%A0%C4%87epanovi%C4%87" title="Vlado Šćepanović">Vlado Šćepanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%90uro_Ostoji%C4%87" title="Đuro Ostojić">Đuro Ostojić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Milojevi%C4%87" title="Dejan Milojević">Dejan Milojević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Predrag_%C5%A0uput" title="Predrag Šuput">Predrag Šuput</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petar_Bo%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Petar Božić">Petar Božić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_House" title="Fred House">Fred House</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vonteego_Cummings" title="Vonteego Cummings">Vonteego Cummings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2006.E2.80.932012">2006–2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2006–2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In tje 2006–07 season, In addition to the sixth consecutive title in Serbia, Partizan won its first Adriatic league trophy, defeating the Serbian club <a href="/wiki/KK_FMP" title="KK FMP">FMP</a>, in the finals. <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Kecman" title="Dušan Kecman">Dušan Kecman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milenko_Tepi%C4%87" title="Milenko Tepić">Milenko Tepić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pekovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Peković">Nikola Peković</a>, with Veličković, Cummings, Perović, Bakić, Bogdanović managed to TOP 16 of Euroleague. Ever since that season Partizan regularly reaches at least the play-off stage of Euroleague. On August 17, 2007 Partizan signed an agreement with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia">Bosnian</a> club <a href="/wiki/KK_Igokea" title="KK Igokea">KK Igokea</a> on technical cooperation, known as "Partizan Igokea". The season 2007-08 was a big come back to the top of European basketball. Partizan Igokea was successful in Euroleague, and strengthened with <a href="/wiki/Milt_Palacio" title="Milt Palacio">Milt Palacio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavko_Vrane%C5%A1" title="Slavko Vraneš">Slavko Vraneš</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cedomir_Vitkovac" title="Čedomir Vitkovac">Čedomir Vitkovac</a> Partizan Igokea knocked out of the competition European champions <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panathinaikos_BC" title="Panathinaikos BC">Panathinaikos</a>, but was stopped in the quarterfinals by <a href="/wiki/Saski_Baskonia" title="Saski Baskonia">Tau Cerámica</a> in a close fought encounter.</p>
<p>On domestic front, Partizan Igokea won the first of four consecutive triple crowns, uniting the trophies in national league, national cup and regional league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2008–09 season Partizan defended all three trophies. New players <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Ra%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Rašić">Aleksandar Rašić</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephane_Lasme" title="Stephane Lasme">Stephane Lasme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vesel%C3%BD" title="Jan Veselý">Jan Veselý</a> played well with Veličković, Tepić, Tripković, Vraneš, Božić and reached the quarterfinals of Euroleague again, where they were eliminated by <a href="/wiki/PBC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PBC CSKA Moscow">CSKA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> On 5 March 2009, Partizan and its fans became record holders, setting a record crowd of 22,567 in a game against Panathinaikos, the highest ever attendance for any basketball game held indoors in Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Dušan Vujošević">Vujošević</a> was given the highest coaching award in Europe, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euroleague_Coach_of_the_Year_Award" title="Euroleague Coach of the Year Award">Euroleague Coach of the Year Award</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and Partizan was chosen by Euroleague to go on tour against NBA teams, becoming one of the selected few clubs to represent European basketball in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="2488" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg/150px-Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg/225px-Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg/300px-Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bo_McCalebb_with_Partizan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bo_McCalebb" title="Bo McCalebb">Bo McCalebb</a> was Partizan's starting point guard during the 2009-10 season.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG/250px-Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG/375px-Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG/500px-Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cibona_vs_Partizan_NLB_League_Final_2010.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cibona vs Partizan in NLB Final in April 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_KK_Partizan_season" title="2009–10 KK Partizan season">2009–10 season</a>, main players from the previous seasons <a href="/wiki/Uro%C5%A1_Tripkovi%C4%87" title="Uroš Tripković">Uroš Tripković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novica_Veli%C4%8Dkovi%C4%87" title="Novica Veličković">Novica Veličković</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milenko_Tepi%C4%87" title="Milenko Tepić">Milenko Tepić</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephane_Lasme" title="Stephane Lasme">Stephane Lasme</a> left the club. Experienced <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Kecman" title="Dušan Kecman">Dušan Kecman</a> returned and <a href="/wiki/Aleks_Mari%C4%87" title="Aleks Marić">Aleks Marić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bo_McCalebb" title="Bo McCalebb">Bo McCalebb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Roberts_(basketball)" title="Lawrence Roberts (basketball)">Lawrence Roberts</a> were brought in. Partizan played better from game to game, and Pionir Hall remained impregnable fortress for many European greats like <a href="/wiki/Anadolu_Efes_S.K." title="Anadolu Efes S.K.">Efes Pilsen</a> or <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona_B%C3%A0squet" title="FC Barcelona Bàsquet">FC Barcelona</a>. Partizan again went to quarterfinals and this time faced Israeli giants <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_B.C." title="Maccabi Tel Aviv B.C.">Maccabi Tel Aviv</a>. Partizan went past their opponent in big style and secured the fourth Final Four of Euroleague.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In the final tournament of Euroleague held in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> Partizan played even with their much richer rivals but was unlucky in both semi-final against <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_B.C." title="Olympiacos B.C.">Olympiacos</a> 80–83 and for 3rd place with <a href="/wiki/PBC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PBC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> 88–90.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Both games were decided in overtime. Partizan again defended national league and cup titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The final game of <a href="/wiki/ABA_League" title="ABA League">Adriatic league</a> in front of the sold-out <a href="/wiki/Arena_Zagreb" title="Arena Zagreb">Arena Zagreb</a> was against longtime rivals from Croatia <a href="/wiki/KK_Cibona" title="KK Cibona">Cibona</a>. Cibona trailed 68–72 with a few seconds left, but back-to-back triples by <a href="/wiki/Marko_Tomas" title="Marko Tomas">Marko Tomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bojan_Bogdanovi%C4%87" title="Bojan Bogdanović">Bojan Bogdanović</a> gave their team a 74–72 lead with just 0.6 seconds left. Cibona players and the crowd already began to celebrate the title, but Partizan had the game's final possession and <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Kecman" title="Dušan Kecman">Dušan Kecman</a> banked in a game-winning triple from midcourt at the buzzer, to make Partizan win another Adriatic League title in front of the shocked crowd and opposition players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the 2010–11 season, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a>, the most successful Partizan coach in history left the club after nine seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vlada_Jovanovi%C4%87" title="Vlada Jovanović">Vlada Jovanović</a>, previously his assistant, became the new head coach. The change in coaching position was followed by changes in playing squad as Marić, McCalebb, Roberts, Vraneš, Rašić left the club. New players were brought in <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Jawai" title="Nathan Jawai">Nathan Jawai</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Gist" title="James Gist">James Gist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Jerrells" title="Curtis Jerrells">Curtis Jerrells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C5%A1ko_Kati%C4%87" title="Raško Katić">Raško Katić</a>. Along with <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vesel%C3%BD" title="Jan Veselý">Jan Veselý</a> these players made the first five, so it was for the first time that Partizan relied mainly on foreign players. The departure of Vujošević initially affected the results, but as the season went on Partizan's play improved and the team again won three trophies - national double and the regional league. In Euroleague, Partizan achieved its main goal and qualified for the Top 16 phase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Again, most of the starters left the team before the 2011–12 season began. Serbian national team players <a href="/wiki/Milan_Ma%C4%8Dvan" title="Milan Mačvan">Milan Mačvan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Raduljica" title="Miroslav Raduljica">Miroslav Raduljica</a> were loaned in, and young players <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lu%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Vladimir Lučić">Vladimir Lučić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Milosavljevi%C4%87" title="Dragan Milosavljević">Dragan Milosavljević</a> got more playing time. Partizan took advantage of the <a href="/wiki/2011_NBA_lockout" title="2011 NBA lockout">NBA lockout</a> to bring in its former player, <a href="/wiki/Center_(basketball)" title="Center (basketball)">center</a> <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pekovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Peković">Nikola Peković</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> With most of the play revolving around him, Partizan got close to securing another Euroleague Top 16 spot, but due to an end of the lockout <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pekovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Peković">Peković</a> returned to the NBA in early December. Without him, Partizan lost all three remaining fixtures and after five consecutive years, failed to qualify further. In the regional Adriatic League, Partizan was stopped in the semifinals, ending its five-year reign in the competition. On the domestic front however, Partizan extended its success, winning another double.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.932014">2012–2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2012–2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The beginning of the 2012–13 season saw the return of <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a> to the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Petar_Bo%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Petar Božić">Petar Božić</a>, long-term captain and the player with the most appearances for the club, retired. <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lu%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Vladimir Lučić">Vladimir Lučić</a> was appointed as captain, and <a href="/wiki/Dragan_Milosavljevi%C4%87" title="Dragan Milosavljević">Dragan Milosavljević</a> became vice-captain. <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Kecman" title="Dušan Kecman">Dušan Kecman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milan_Ma%C4%8Dvan" title="Milan Mačvan">Milan Mačvan</a> were also among the players who left. The squad was rejuvenated, with the oldest player <a href="/wiki/Marko_%C4%8Cakarevi%C4%87" title="Marko Čakarević">Marko Čakarević</a> being just 24 years old. Initially, the results in <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Euroleague" title="2012–13 Euroleague">Euroleague</a> suffered, with Partizan's inexperienced squad being knocked-out of the group stage. After mixed performances in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Liga_ABA" title="2012–13 Liga ABA">ABA League</a> regular season, Partizan performed well in the final four, winning its sixth regional title, and securing another season in <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">Euroleague</a>. In the Serbian championship, Partizan successfully defended the trophy and brought its record to twenty national titles, the last twelve being consecutive. The 2013-14 season was marked by the rise of young players such as <a href="/wiki/D%C4%81vis_Bert%C4%81ns" title="Dāvis Bertāns">Dāvis Bertāns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogdan_Bogdanovi%C4%87_(basketball)" title="Bogdan Bogdanović (basketball)">Bogdan Bogdanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joffrey_Lauvergne" title="Joffrey Lauvergne">Joffrey Lauvergne</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9o_Westermann" title="Léo Westermann">Léo Westermann</a>. Despite failure at the Final Four of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_ABA_League" title="2013–14 ABA League">Adriatic League</a>, Partizan finished the season by winning its thirteenth consecutive title, again defeating their archrivals <a href="/wiki/KK_Crvena_zvezda" title="KK Crvena zvezda">Red Star Belgrade</a> by 3-1 in the final series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.93present">2014–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2014–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014–15 season, Partizan finished fourth in the regular season of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_ABA_League" title="2014–15 ABA League">Adriatic League</a>, only to be eliminated in the playoff semifinals. Partizan was also eliminated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radivoj_Kora%C4%87_Cup_2014-15" title="Radivoj Korać Cup 2014-15">Serbian Cup</a> and failed to defend the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Basketball_League_of_Serbia" title="2014–15 Basketball League of Serbia">Serbian League</a> title, losing to Red Star Belgrade in the final series. Without a single trophy won, the season was the worst in fourteen years.</p>
<p>The summer of 2015 included many organizational and roster changes. The board of directors suggested <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Pekovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Peković">Nikola Peković</a>, former Partizan player, for the next team president, after the resignation of <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Danilovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Danilović">Predrag Danilović</a>. Soon after that, Petar Božić was offered a head coach position, with longtime head coach Vujošević departing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Several team veterans and foreign players also left the club, with <a href="/wiki/Vanja_Marinkovi%C4%87" title="Vanja Marinković">Vanja Marinković</a> becoming the new team captain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of 2016, Partizan resign contract with Petar Božić after very bad results (worst half-season in Partizan history). Partizan new coach was <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_D%C5%BEiki%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Džikić">Aleksandar Džikić</a>, who managed to finish <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_ABA_League" title="2015–16 ABA League">Adriatic League</a> season on 5th position, and finish the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Basketball_League_of_Serbia" title="2015–16 Basketball League of Serbia">Serbian League</a> as a second, losing to Red Star Belgrade in finals. In 2016/2017 Partizan is playing in <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Champions_League" title="Basketball Champions League">Basketball Champions League</a>, after withdrawal from <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Eurocup" title="Eurocup">Eurocup</a> (after blackmail from Serbian basketball association, and Fiba). The current team captain is <a href="/wiki/Novica_Veli%C4%8Dkovi%C4%87" title="Novica Veličković">Novica Veličković</a></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grobari" title="Grobari">Grobari</a></div>
<p><b>Grobari</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic" title="Serbian Cyrillic">Serbian Cyrillic</a>: Гробари, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>: The Gravediggers) are supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> football club <a href="/wiki/FK_Partizan" title="FK Partizan">Partizan</a>. They generally support all clubs within the <b><a href="/wiki/JSD_Partizan" title="JSD Partizan">Sports Association Partizan</a></b>, especially football and basketball club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasons"><a href="/wiki/Season_(sports)" title="Season (sports)">Seasons</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KK_Partizan_seasons" title="KK Partizan seasons">KK Partizan seasons</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_records">Awards and records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Awards and records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/KK_Partizan_accomplishments_and_records" title="KK Partizan accomplishments and records">KK Partizan accomplishments and records</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_arenas">Home arenas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Home arenas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:488px;max-width:488px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2848" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg/220px-Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg/330px-Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg/440px-Hala_Pionir_Beograd.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Hall Aleksandar Nikolić, home arena of the KK Partizan since 1992.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:262px;max-width:262px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arena111.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="318" data-file-width="500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Arena111.jpg/260px-Arena111.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Arena111.jpg/390px-Arena111.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Arena111.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Kombank Arena, home arena for Euroleague games.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Partizan play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Hall_Aleksandar_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Hall Aleksandar Nikolić">Hall Aleksandar Nikolić</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> municipality of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palilula_Belgrade" title="Palilula Belgrade">Palilula</a>. The arena, then named Pionir Hall, was built in 1973 in eleven months, by <a href="/wiki/Energoprojekt_holding" title="Energoprojekt holding">Energoprojekt</a>. Basketball was popular in Yugoslavia at the time, and although Hall Aleksandar iIkolić hosted many different sport events (<a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a>) it became known as a basketball arena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It has a seating capacity of 5,878.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hall_Aleksandar_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Hall Aleksandar Nikolić">Hall Aleksandar Nikolić</a> is also the home of Partizan's main rival <a href="/wiki/KK_Crvena_zvezda" title="KK Crvena zvezda">Red Star Belgrade</a>. In the first twenty-three years (1945–1968), the club played their home games at Open basketball courts on <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_Fortress" title="Belgrade Fortress">Belgrade Fortress</a> before moving to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_Hall_%22Ranko_%C5%BDeravica%22" title='Sports Hall "Ranko Žeravica"'>Hall Ranko Žeravica</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> For 24 seasons (1968–1992), Partizan played their home games at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_Hall_%22Ranko_%C5%BDeravica%22" title='Sports Hall "Ranko Žeravica"'>Hall Ranko Žeravica</a>, located in Belgrade municipality of <a href="/wiki/New_Belgrade" title="New Belgrade">New Belgrade</a>. In the 2008–09 season, Partizan played their home games of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euroleague" title="Euroleague">Euroleague</a> Top 16 in the <a href="/wiki/Kombank_Arena" title="Kombank Arena">Kombank Arena</a>. On 5 March 2009 against Greek team Panathinaikos, a record crowd of 22,567 was set for the Euroleague.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_coaches">Head coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Head coaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1996" data-file-width="1894" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg/150px-Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg/225px-Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg/300px-Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a> is the most successful coach in club's history.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_KK_Partizan_head_coaches" title="List of KK Partizan head coaches">List of KK Partizan head coaches</a></div>
<p>There have been twenty-six <a href="/wiki/Head_coach" title="Head coach">head coaches</a> for Partizan since the founding of the club in 1945. The first head coach was <a href="/wiki/Bo%C5%BEo_Grkini%C4%87" title="Božo Grkinić">Božo Grkinić</a> who coached Partizan for two seasons. The first coach to bring Partizan an official trophy was <a href="/wiki/Borislav_%C4%86orkovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Ćorković">Borislav Ćorković</a>. He won <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Basketball_League" title="Yugoslav Basketball League">Yugoslav League</a> with Partizan in 1976. Club won the first international trophy in 1978, while being coached by <a href="/wiki/Ranko_%C5%BDeravica" title="Ranko Žeravica">Ranko Žeravica</a>. <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Željko Obradović">Željko Obradović</a> lead the club to the most significant trophy, <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">Euroleague</a> in 1992. <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Vujo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Duško Vujošević">Duško Vujošević</a> is the most successful coach in the club's history. In his four stints with Partizan he won a total of twenty-three trophies. <a href="/wiki/Borislav_Stankovi%C4%87" title="Borislav Stanković">Borislav Stanković</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ranko_%C5%BDeravica" title="Ranko Žeravica">Ranko Žeravica</a> are members of <a href="/wiki/FIBA_Hall_of_Fame" title="FIBA Hall of Fame">FIBA Hall of Fame</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> while <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Nikolić">Aleksandar Nikolić</a> is a member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Basketball Hall of Fame">Basketball Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Nikolić">Nikolić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1an_Ivkovi%C4%87" title="Dušan Ivković">Dušan Ivković</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDeljko_Obradovi%C4%87" title="Željko Obradović">Željko Obradović</a> have been named among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50_Greatest_Euroleague_Contributors" title="50 Greatest Euroleague Contributors">50 Greatest Euroleague Contributors</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Partizan has won thirty-four domestic trophies, including twenty-one <a href="/wiki/Basketball_League_of_Serbia" title="Basketball League of Serbia">championships</a>, of which the last twelve were won consecutively, and thirteen cups, of which the last five were won consecutively. They have also won six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liga_ABA" title="Liga ABA">Adriatic championships</a>, first five of them consecutive. In European competitions in the late 1970s, they won two back-to-back <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kora%C4%87_Cup" title="Korać Cup">Korać Cups</a> in 1978 and 1979. They also won another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kora%C4%87_Cup" title="Korać Cup">Korać Cup</a> in 1989. In 1992, Partizan won the club's first – and to date only – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euroleague" title="Euroleague">Euroleague</a> title, downing <a href="/wiki/Joventut_Badalona" title="Joventut Badalona">Joventut Badalona</a> 70–71 on a miraculous buzzer-beater by <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_%C4%90or%C4%91evi%C4%87" title="Aleksandar Đorđević">Aleksandar Đorđević</a>, which ranks among the most amazing shots in European basketball history. Overall, Partizan has won forty-four trophies, which makes it the most successful basketball club in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_European_and_worldwide_competitions">In European and worldwide competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: In European and worldwide competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/KK_Partizan_in_European_and_worldwide_competitions" title="KK Partizan in European and worldwide competitions">KK Partizan in European and worldwide competitions</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Matches_against_NBA_teams">Matches against NBA teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KK_Partizan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Matches against NBA teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Partizan is the first and so far only club from Serbia that played games against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA" title="NBA">NBA</a> teams. On the <a href="/wiki/2009_Euroleague_American_Tour" title="2009 Euroleague American Tour">2009 Euroleague American Tour</a>, Partizan played against <a href="/wiki/Denver_Nuggets" title="Denver Nuggets">Denver Nuggets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Suns" title="Phoenix Suns">Phoenix Suns</a>.</p>
